Multi-dimensional data in Pandas with panels and multi-indexed dataframes.

Posted on Thu 08 June 2017 in Posts

Multi-indexing and panels use for multi-dimensioanal data in Pandas¶

Link To Data Used: [http://www.yourfilelink.com/get.php?fid=1367921]

DataReader Documentation [https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#google-finance]

In [49]:
import pandas as pd
import pandas_datareader as data
import datetime
In [50]:
df_players = pd.read_csv("FullData.csv")
In [51]:
df_players.head(3)

In [52]:
df_players["Club_Position"]  = df_players["Club_Position"].astype("category")
In [53]:
df_players["Club"] = df_players["Club"].astype("category")
In [54]:
df_players["Nationality"] = df_players["Nationality"].astype("category")
In [55]:
df_players.set_index(keys=["Club_Position","Nationality","Club"],inplace=True)

With set_index() one can choose columns which will be used for indexing. keys argument will take a string(single column name) or a list of stings for multi-indexing, order of the list will be followed for indexing too.

One will notice even though multi-indexing is used,the dataframe is not properly categorised. This can be troubleshot by sorting the indices.

In [57]:
df_players.sort_index(inplace=True)

With inplace=True the dataframe will be overwritten. Lets see what changes are made now:

Few things to take note of:-

  1. inplace parameter is not available here, therefore one has to over write manually.
  2. multi-indexing is maintained after transposong too,which is obvious to do.
  3. notice the change in parameter of .ix[ ]

Few other interesting and alternative methods available:

In [72]:
df_players = df_players.swaplevel(i=-1,j=-2)

Lets get into panels now:¶

In [78]:
start = datetime.date(2015,1,1)
end = datetime.date(2017,1,1)

Don't forget to check documentation of datareader,it's easy enough to understand at once.

In [79]:

Notice one has to start with referencing "Items axis". Imagine this as bunch of dataframe, here the dataframes are referred as - 'Open', 'High', 'Low', 'Close', 'Volume'. Now, what if one wants to refer the dataframes with the company names('AAPL', 'GOOG', 'MSFT'). Lets see what options we have:

In [99]:
data_stock_t = data_stock.transpose(2,1,0)
data_stock_t

Starting with transpose() arguments passed here are the axes indices of the previous state of panel in the order in which one wants the panel axes to be in next state. And for swapaxes() it is quite intuituive and easy to guess, just pass axes you want to swap. Options for swapaxes() are - 'items','minor' & 'major'.

As one learns about panels and multi-indexing, one can easily conclude both the techniques can be used alternatively. So, lets about converting one format to the other:

In [108]:
data_stock_f = data_stock.to_frame()
